**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

**All following Reddit news posts are from the subreddit r/politics.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:
Breaking political news
Opinion pieces and editorials
Legislation and policy discussions
Elections, political figures, and government actions

It's moderated to focus on U.S.-centric content and generally avoids memes or low-effort posts. The subreddit can have a progressive or liberal-leaning tone, depending on the community's engagement, though it hosts a range of political perspectives.

**Step 1 (logic-heavy)**

Define the Categories: 

Read through the titles of hundreds of news articles and think carefully.  Use your memory fully. Define major areas, and define specific topics under each area, in a hierarchical way. Every news article should have its best-fitting category. There should be two hierarchical tiers (area, topic), instead of three, and then we get down to individual articles. You should consider this very carefully, making the categories the most helpful for human cognition. Control the total number of areas to 5-8, depending on how diverse and complex the topics are. **AREA 1: EXECUTIVE BRANCH OPERATIONS & INTERNAL DYNAMICS**

**Topic 1.1: The Epstein Files Fallout and DOJ/FBI Tensions**

A significant and destabilizing internal crisis is unfolding within the administration's top law enforcement agencies, centered on the handling of the "Epstein files" [1, 2]. The conflict is an acute intra-agency feud between Attorney General Pam Bondi and Deputy FBI Director Dan Bongino. Tensions reportedly erupted into a "White House blowup" after the Department of Justice issued a specific memo regarding the Epstein case, creating a direct clash between the two leaders [3, 4]. The fallout from this confrontation has severely roiled relations between the Attorney General and the Deputy FBI Director. In the immediate aftermath, Bongino has been reported as absent from his duties at the Bureau and has privately told associates that he is actively considering resignation, signaling a high-level fracture within federal law enforcement that could have cascading effects on agency morale and operations [5, 6].

**Topic 1.2: Administration Personnel and Agency Management**

The administration is executing major structural and personnel changes across the federal government. A previously reported and controversial plan to abolish the Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) has now been officially scrapped, according to the Washington Post [1]. This reversal comes amid other aggressive actions, including a large-scale staff reduction at the State Department, which terminated the employment of more than 1,300 staff members on a single Friday [2]. In a more opaque development, the administration has issued what one report characterizes as "non-denial denials on Emil Bove." The headlines do not provide the necessary context on Bove's role or the substance of the issue, but the phrasing suggests a carefully managed public relations situation that warrants further monitoring [3].

**AREA 2: IMMIGRATION POLICY & ENFORCEMENT**

**Topic 2.1: Enforcement Actions, Protests, and Casualties**

Immigration enforcement has intensified dramatically, marked by violent confrontations, civilian casualties, and a new, broad federal justification for detention. A "Border Czar" has publicly declared that an individual's "physical appearance" alone is now considered sufficient grounds for ICE agents to detain and question them, explicitly stating that agents "don't need probable cause" for such an action [1]. These aggressive enforcement operations have triggered widespread protests, one of which saw an individual allegedly fire a pistol at federal immigration agents in California [2]. Federal raids have been linked to severe and fatal outcomes, including the death of a cannabis farm worker a day after what was described as a "chaotic" raid, and another man being placed on life support due to an injury sustained during a raid in Ventura County [3, 4]. The social impact is palpable, with the bishop of a major Catholic diocese granting parishioners an exemption from attending Mass due to pervasive fears of ICE raids [5]. A separate legal filing confirms the administration has been using the controversial Canary Mission database to identify and target students for deportation [6].

**Topic 2.2: Detention Conditions and Legal Challenges**

The administration’s immigration agenda is facing significant legal setbacks and public condemnation over detention conditions. In a major legal ruling, a federal court has blocked President Trump's order seeking to end birthright citizenship. The court also certified a nationwide class to protect all babies impacted by the policy, representing a substantial blow to a cornerstone of the President's platform [1]. Simultaneously, severe allegations have surfaced regarding conditions at a detention facility nicknamed 'Alligator Alcatraz.' Detainees have described "worms in food" and "sewage near beds" in harrowing reports of an inhumane environment [2]. These accounts have been amplified by the Archbishop of Miami, who publicly shredded praise of the facility from administration allies, calling such statements "unbecoming of public officials" [3]. Alongside these issues, the administration has also moved to cut access for undocumented immigrants to an unspecified range of federally funded programs [4].

**AREA 3: BUDGET, ECONOMY, & TRADE**

**Topic 3.1: Tariffs, Trade Policy, and International Economic Relations**

The administration’s tariff-focused trade policy is producing distinct fiscal and diplomatic outcomes. The U.S. Treasury reported an unexpected budget surplus for the month of June, a development that is being attributed directly to a significant surge in federal tariff receipts [1]. On the international front, this tariff pressure may be creating new negotiating leverage. The administration is reportedly engaged in substantive talks with India for a new trade deal, with discussions including the possibility of reducing tariffs to below the 20% level [2].

**Topic 3.2: Federal Budget, Regulation, and Economic Impact**

President Trump's proposed federal funding cuts are encountering potential headwinds from within the Republican party, creating uncertainty about their viability in Congress [1]. The administration's "megabill" is facing sharp criticism from Democrats; Rep. Summer Lee, for instance, has characterized it as the "biggest wealth transfer in history" and a mechanism fueling America's "slide into plutocratic authoritarianism" [2]. Social service organizations are raising alarms that these proposed cuts will overwhelm the nation's food banks with newly hungry individuals [3]. In a separate but related economic development, a Texas judge has vacated the Consumer Financial Protection Bureau's (CFPB) ban on the reporting of medical debt, a significant regulatory rollback [4].

**AREA 4: DISASTER RESPONSE & ENVIRONMENTAL POLICY**

**Topic 4.1: Texas Flooding and Federal Emergency Response**

The federal response to catastrophic flooding in Texas has become a flashpoint for intense scrutiny and criticism. The administration's approach is being condemned, particularly as it follows the recently abandoned proposal to eliminate FEMA, the nation's primary disaster agency [1]. ## 5. Domestic Politics, Law, & Society

### 5.1 Civil Rights, Social Policy, and Court Rulings
The Trump administration's relationship with higher education has become overtly hostile, with Harvard University a primary target. Facing direct "funding threats and accusations of ideological bias" from the President, the university is now reportedly considering the establishment of a "Center for Conservative Scholarship" as a potential strategic response [1, 2]. In a separate matter with broad social implications, schools nationwide are bracing for a potential "wave of parents seeking opt-outs" from unspecified curricula or activities following a recent Supreme Court ruling [3]. On LGBTQ issues, reports state that the GOP has erased all mentions of bisexual individuals from the official government webpages for the Stonewall National Monument [4].

### 5.2 Partisan Politics and Intra-Party Conflicts
Visible fractures are appearing within the conservative movement and the Republican party. The administration's handling of the Epstein files has generated significant blowback, with attendees at a recent conservative conference openly "ripping Trump" on the issue [1]. This discontent is echoed by some far-right influencers and figures in the "manosphere" who are reportedly turning on the President [2, 3]. President Trump himself issued what one outlet called a "frantic new threat" to the GOP via a Truth Social post, signaling direct pressure on the party establishment [4]. Separately, a major political battle is escalating in New York, where the "financial crowd" is building a large "Anti-Mamdani war chest" to oppose a progressive candidate. Senator Bernie Sanders claims the effort is driven by billionaire fears of a nationwide progressive movement [5].

### 5.3 Federal-State Relations and State-Level Policy
Friction between the federal government and several states is increasing over a range of policy issues. The Trump administration has initiated a lawsuit against the state of California over the cost of eggs [1]. In Missouri, the state's Republican Governor has signed a repeal of a voter-approved paid sick leave law, a move critics decried as a "slap in the face" to workers [2]. In New York, Hochul is warning of potentially "draconian cuts" to the state budget, attributing the looming shortfall to a federal policy referred to only as "OBBBA" [3]. In Oklahoma, State Superintendent Ryan Walters has mandated that educators relocating from states he has labeled as "woke" must complete a new assessment before they can teach in Oklahoma schools [4].

The political battlefield is increasingly digital, with new reports on biased AI, online harassment campaigns, and allegations of subverted public discourse. A report on Elon Musk's Grok chatbot claims the AI has been designed to specifically search for the billionaire's own views before it formulates answers to user questions, raising significant bias concerns [1]. In another area of online activity, a Rolling Stone report indicates that "Reddit Trolls" are weaponizing government agencies to target and harass online creators [2]. Separately, the Missouri Attorney General has made the public claim that AI chatbots are actively "undermining Trump record," though the specific mechanism for this alleged undermining is not detailed in the headline [3].

## 6. Foreign Policy & International Relations

### 6.1 Ukraine & Russia Policy
The administration's posture towards the war in Ukraine may be undergoing a significant evolution. According to a Politico report, President Trump is now actively weighing a new aid package for Ukraine, a notable potential shift in policy [1]. This development occurs as the administration continues to face sharp criticism from congressional Democrats. House Minority Leader Hakeem Jeffries, for instance, recently accused the Trump administration of "playing footsie" with Russia, suggesting a perception of an overly conciliatory or ambiguous stance toward the Kremlin [2]. This situation highlights a potential conflict between new policy considerations and entrenched political perceptions of the administration's foreign policy.

**References:**
[1] Trump weighs new Ukraine aid package, https://www.politico.com/news/2025/07/11/trump-new-ukraine-aid-package-00448547  
[2] Jeffries says Trump administration ‘playing footsie’ with Russia, https://thehill.com/homenews/house/5392229-hakeem-jeffries-donald-trump-russia-ukraine-war/  

### 6.2 Diplomatic Relations and Global Engagements
The administration’s foreign policy is generating notable friction with key partners, alongside some unexpected diplomatic outreach. The President of Brazil has publicly rebuked President Trump over a tariff threat and critical comments made about former Brazilian President Bolsonaro [1]. Similarly, the government of Nigeria has pushed back against a U.S. proposal to send Venezuelan deportees to their country, stating, "We have enough problems of our own" [2]. Ahead of a planned state visit to the United Kingdom, reports suggest that President Trump may be denied the traditional honor of addressing Parliament [3]. In a different theater, a U.S. mission in Congo, which was intended to advance a Trump-led deal, has reportedly "unravelled"; the headline provides no further detail on the nature of the deal or the cause of its failure [4]. In contrast to these tensions, a previously "shunned" leader of Myanmar is said to be "thrilled" after receiving direct contact from President Trump in the form of a letter concerning tariffs [5].
